What is Anupam's age? c) Twenty-seven ЁЯУЭ Word Meanings & Annotations Main Word	Meaning & Explanation This life is neither long in length nor high in quality	Self-criticism by Anupam, the narrator, indicating his life is insignificant both in quantity and quality. Like fruitless buds	A metaphor used by Anupam to describe his life as one that never blossomed into success, like buds that never became fruits. Angapuri	Goddess Annapurna (Goddess of food). Gajanan	Refers to Kartikeya, the younger son of Goddess Durga. Used humorously.

Even today, if you see me, you'll think IтАЩm the younger brother of Gajanan on Annapurna's lap	Anupam ironically describes his weak and dependent appearance. Phalgu	A hidden (subterranean) river in the Gaya region of India, with water underneath but sand on top. Like the sand of Phalgu, he absorbed the whole family within himself	Anupam says this about his uncle who silently took responsibility for the family. Ganbhasha	A single-mouth water container or cell. Antahpur	Inner quarters of a household (womenтАЩs quarters). Swayambara	A ceremony where a woman chooses her own husband. Gurguri	A long-stemmed traditional smoking pipe (from Persian origin). Tied hookah	A hookah made of coconut shell used by common people. Umedari	Seeking help, usually for a job or livelihood. In the desert of leisure, once their familyтАЩs pot of prosperity was full	Refers to the once-prosperous heritage of KalyaniтАЩs family. Western Andaman Islands	Refers metaphorically to a remote part of India. Konnagar	A coastal island in the Bay of Bengal within Indian territory, associated with exile during the Swadeshi movement. Narrative / Story Section: Today, I am only twenty-seven years old. This life is neither great in terms of length nor in terms of quality. Yet, it has a special value. It is like that flower upon whose bosom a bee had come and sat, and the history of that footstep has clung to the very core of its life like the pit of a fruit in the middle. That small historyтАФI will write it down in a small form. Those who do not mistake the small for the insignificant will understand its essence (rasa).
---
clung to the very core of its life like the pit of a fruit in the middle. That small historyтАФI will write it down in a small form. Those who do not mistake the small for the insignificant will understand its essence (rasa). I have passed all the college examinations. In my childhood, scholars used to compare my beautiful eyes to the flame of the silk cotton tree and the unripe mango fruit, thereby mocking me. I used to feel very embarrassed by it then; but as I grew older, I thought that if rebirth exists, then beauty on my face and mockery in the scholars' mouths seem to manifest instantly just like that. My father was once poor. Practicing law, he earned a lot of money, but he never got a moment's leisure to enjoy it. The half he left behind at his death was his first vacation. I was quite young then. I grew up in my mother's lap. My mother is a girl from the household; therefore, she never forgets, nor does she let me forget, that we are wealthy. I was a child carried in armsтАФperhaps that is why, ultimately, my age never fully matured. Even now, seeing me, one might think I am like the younger brother of Gajanana (Ganesha), sitting in the lap of Annapurna. My real guardian is my maternal uncle (Mama). He is only about six years older than me. But like the sand of the Phalgu river, he has absorbed our entire family within his heart. There is no juice (rasa) to be had from even a single creeper (gana-bhusha) here without disturbing him. For this reason, I never have to think about anything. Any father of a daughter will admit that I am a suitable match. I don't even smoke tobacco. There is no fuss about being a good man, so I am simply a good man. I have the ability to obey my mother's ordersтАФactually, I don't have the ability not to obey. I am prepared to live under the rule of the zenana (inner quarters) just like that; if any girl is to choose her groom herself, she should remember this virtue.
---
ordersтАФactually, I don't have the ability not to obey. I am prepared to live under the rule of the zenana (inner quarters) just like that; if any girl is to choose her groom herself, she should remember this virtue. My connections come from a very big house (wealthy family). But my Mama, who is my principal agent of fate in this world, had a particular opinion about marriage. He doesn't like the daughter of a rich man. The girl who will come to our house must come walking barefoot, this is what he wants. Yet, his attachment to money is ingrained in his bones and marrow. He wants a girl who has no money but won't mind giving money. Someone who can be exploited, but when she comes to the house, instead of jaggery (gud), if she is given tobacco in a broken hookah bowl, she won't complain. My Hari works in Kanpur. During his leave, he came to Calcutta and stirred up my mind. He said, "Brother, if you say so, there is a very fine girl." I had just passed my MA (Master of Arts) a short while ago. As far ahead as the eye can see, the path of life is covered in dust; there are no exams, no hopes, no job; no thought even about looking after oneself, no education, no desireтАФbecause inside is Mother and outside is Mama. In the desert of this leisure, my heart was then seeing the mirage of a woman of the worldтАФa vision in the sky, her breath in the air, her secret words rustling in the trees. Just then, Hari came and said, "If the girl says yes, thenтАФ" My body and mind started trembling like the new shoots of a Bakul grove in a spring breeze, beginning to weave light and shade. Hari was a man of taste, he had the skill to describe things with rasa, and my mind was thirsty. I told Hari, "First, try putting the matter before Mama." Hari is incomparable at arranging things. That's why he is welcome everywhere. Mama also doesn't like to let him go when he gets him. The matter came up in his drawing room (Baitok). He cared more about the girl's father's background than the girl herself. He wants to know exactly the kind of financial condition the father has.
---
let him go when he gets him. The matter came up in his drawing room (Baitok). He cared more about the girl's father's background than the girl herself. He wants to know exactly the kind of financial condition the father has. Once, Lakshmi's blessings were abundant in this family lineage. Now, it can be said to be empty, although there's still a little left in the basement. It's not easy to maintain family prestige by living in the country, so he has gone west and lives there. He lives there like a poor householder. Apart from one daughter, he has nothing else. Therefore, they won't hesitate to completely overturn Lakshmi's pot from behind. Well, that's fine. But hearing that the girl is only fifteen, Mama's mind grew heavy. Is there any fault in the lineage? No, there's no faultтАФthe father just can't find a groom worthy of his daughter anywhere. The bridegroom's market is highly expensive these days, and furthermore, the bride is worn out and broken, so the father is just waiting patientlyтАФbut the girl's youth isn't waiting patiently. Anyway, Hari's charming description had merit. Mama's mind softened. The preliminary arrangements for the marriage went smoothly. Mama considers the whole world outside Calcutta to be part of the Andaman Islands. Once, for some special work, he had even gone as far as Kharagpur. Mama's wish was to go and see the girl with his own eyes. I couldn't gather the courage to prepare for it. My paternal uncle Binu was sent to bless the bride. I can rely entirely on his taste and skill, like sixteen annas (the full amount). Uncle Binu returned and said, "Not bad, hey\! Pure gold\!" Uncle Binu's language is extremely blunt. Where we would say 'wonderful', he says 'chalan-sai' (fitting/proper). Therefore, I understood that there is no conflict between my fate and the five arrows of the god of love (Kamadeva).
---
Where we would say 'wonderful', he says 'chalan-sai' (fitting/proper). Therefore, I understood that there is no conflict between my fate and the five arrows of the god of love (Kamadeva). Needless to say, on the occasion of the marriage, the bride's party had to come to Calcutta. How much Shambhu Nath Babu trusted Hari was proved by the fact that three days before the wedding, he saw me with his own eyes and blessed me before leaving. His age is somewhere around forty. His hair is cut short, and his mustache has just started to show a curl. He is indeed handsome. If you see him in a crowd, he is the kind of face that catches the eye first. I hope he was happy to see me. It's hard to tell, because he is very quiet. The few words he spoke seemed to be said without much force. Mama's mouth was then running loose in holiday chatterтАФbragging that our place is in no way inferior to anyone else's in the city, he was propagating this in various contexts. Shambhu Nath Babu didn't agree with this talk at allтАФhe didn't utter even a single "yes" or "hmm" anywhere. If I were in his place, I would have been furious, but it's hard to stop Mama. Seeing Shambhu Nath Babu's silence, Mama thought the man was completely lifeless, without any spark. Even if there were other merits in the bride, lacking spark was a fault. Therefore, Mama was secretly pleased. When Shambhu Nath Babu got up to leave, Mama briefly bid him farewell from above (upstairs) and didn't even go down to help him into the carriage. The matter of the bride had been completely settled between both parties. Mama prides himself on being extraordinarily clever. In conversation, he leaves no gap anywhere. The amount of money was already fixed, and then the weight of the ornaments and the price of gold were also completely settled in advance.
---
settled between both parties. Mama prides himself on being extraordinarily clever. In conversation, he leaves no gap anywhere. The amount of money was already fixed, and then the weight of the ornaments and the price of gold were also completely settled in advance. I myself was not involved in all these talks; I didn't know what debts or credits were settled. I knew in my heart that this gross part was also a major aspect of the marriage, and he would not cheat even a bit regarding that aspect's burden. Actually, Mama considers himself a seasoned person and the main pride of our entire family. Wherever we have any connection, he will win battles of wit everywhere; this is a foregone conclusion. Therefore, even if we are not in need and the other party is in great need, he will still winтАФfor the stubbornness of our family, let whoever survives, survive, and whoever dies, die. The Haldi (turmeric) ceremony was unimaginably grand. The expenditure went so high that the accountants had to be called in to take stock. Remembering how the other party would have to incur extra expenses to bid farewell to the carriers, Mama and Ma laughed heartily together. With bands, flutes, enthusiastic concerts, and whatever loud sounds there areтАФaltogether mixing into a barbaric cacophony like an elephant trampling the lotus grove of Saraswati (goddess of music), I entered the wedding house. It seemed as if my body, adorned with garlands and haldi, was walking about encased in ornaments, as if trying to clearly demonstrate to the future father-in-law the value of his son-in-law and prepare for a confrontation.
---
house. It seemed as if my body, adorned with garlands and haldi, was walking about encased in ornaments, as if trying to clearly demonstrate to the future father-in-law the value of his son-in-law and prepare for a confrontation. Mama was not happy entering the wedding house. Firstly, the courtyard was too crowded for the groom's party's accommodation, and secondly, all the arrangements were of a merely middling standard. Moreover, Shambhu Nath Babu's behaviour was extremely cold. He has no shortage of ruined appearance. He had no words on his lips, a towel tied around his waist, a broken necktie, a torn shirt, and a huge body. If one of his lawyer friends hadn't gone and bowed humbly, greeting him with a smile of humility and faltering speech, accompanied by the rhythmic clapping of the concert party, and hadn't blessed each of the groom's party members repeatedly and profusely, things would have gone awry from the very beginning. A little while after I sat down in the gathering, Mama called Shambhu Nath Babu aside to the next room. I don't know what was said, but after a short while, Shambhu Nath Babu came to me and said, "Babaji, you need to come this way once\!" Here's the matter: Everyone might not, but he certainly wouldn't be cheated by anyone somehow. His fear was that his daughter-in-law might cheat him regarding the ornamentsтАФonce the marriage ceremony was over, there would be no remedy for such cheating. From the signs of haggling and bargaining regarding house rent, dowry, and farewell gifts, Mama had decidedтАФrelying solely on this man's word regarding giving and taking would not do. That's why he had brought the house's security guard (sekar) along as well. Going to the next room, I saw Mama sitting on a cot, and the sekar beside him holding his shaving bowl, whetstone, etc. Shambhu Nath Babu said to me, "Your Mama says he will check and verify all the bride's ornaments before the marriage rituals begin. What do you say to that?" I bowed my head and remained silent. Mama said, "What will he say? Whatever I say, will happen." Shambhu Nath Babu, looking at me, said, "So, is that settled?

Mama then noted down the list of ornaments in his notebook, checking against what was shown later; nothing was found short. After calculating, he saw that in terms of number, price, and weight, these ornaments were much more than what was supposed to be given. Among the ornaments was a pair of earrings. Shambhu Nath handed that pair to the sekar and said, "Check this pair once." The sekar said, "This is foreign stuff, Ma'am, there's very little gold in it." His face reddened with affection. The poor man wanted to cheat him, but he wouldn't be cheated; he missed out on the joy of this auspicious union and incurred some extra debt on top of it. With an extremely heavy heart, he said, "Anupam, go, sit in the gathering."

Birth Details Birth Date: 7th May, 1861 (25th Baishakh, 1268 Bengali Era) Birthplace: Jorasanko, Kolkata, India. Lineage Father's Name: Maharshi Debendranath Tagore. Mother's Name: Sarada Devi. ) Birthplace: Jorasanko, Kolkata, India. Lineage Father's Name: Maharshi Debendranath Tagore. Mother's Name: Sarada Devi. Grandfather's Name: Prince Dwarkanath Tagore. Educational Life Rabindranath studied at various educational institutions like Oriental Seminary, Normal School, Bengal Academy, St. Xavier's School, etc., in his early days, but he couldn't complete his school education. Although he went to England at the age of 17 to study law, he couldn't complete the course. However, he had no lack of knowledge gained through home tutoring. Profession / Career Life From 1884, on his father's orders, Rabindranath was engaged in managing family estates and, from 1890, he oversaw zamindari (landlord) affairs in various regions of the country. Through this, he resided for a long time in Shilaidah, Kushtia, and Shahzadpur, Sirajganj. He was a painter, an inquisitive world traveler, a skilled organizer, and an extraordinary educator and thinker. Although he was reluctant towards institutional education, he was the founder and establisher of the university named 'Visva-Bharati'. Literary Works Poetry Collections: Manasi , Sonar Tori , Chitra , Chaitali , Khonika , Naivedya , Gitanjali , Balaka , Purabi , Punshcha , Bichitra , Sanchaiti , Janmdin , Shesh Lekha , etc., are particularly noteworthy. Novels: Chokher Bali , Gora , Ghare Baire , Chaturanga , Noukadubi , Yogayog , Rajarshi , Shesher Kobita , etc. Plays: Achalayatan , Chirakumar Satty , Dakghar , Mukut , Muktir Upay , Muktadhara , Raktakarabi , Raja , etc. Essay Collections: Bichitra Prabandha , Shiksha , Kalanter , Shobhyotar Shoktikot , etc. Travelogues: Japan Jatri , Pather Sanchoy , Persye , Russia'r Chithi , Europe Jatri'r Diary , Europe Probashi'r Patra , etc. Awards and Honors

Reading Introduction "Aporichita" was first published in the Kartik issue of 1321 Bengali Year (1914) of the monthly magazine 'Sabujpatra', edited by Promoth Choudhury. It was first included in the collection 'Galpasaptak' and later in the third volume of 'Galpaguccha' (1927). The story "Aporichita" narrates the tale of a woman named Kalyani, who, under the guise of the adjective 'unacquainted', possesses a strong personality. Tagore had previously written stories about women who became ruthless victims of the inhuman dowry system. However, in this story, he first presented the narrative of joint resistance by men and women against the dowry system. In this story, the independent outlook and conduct of the father Shambhu Nath Sen and his daughter Kalyani confront the cruel and entrenched dowry system of society. The story gains significance through the father's strong resistance and the awakening and expression of Kalyani's personality, enriched with national consciousness. "Aporichita" is a story narrated in the first person. The narrator, Anupam, is a young Bengali man from the second decade of the 20th century, amidst the times bordering the war, who, despite acquiring a higher university degree, is personality-less and merely a puppet dependent on family structures. Looking at him, one might think he is just a child clinging to his mother's lap. It is on the occasion of his marriage that the story reaches its peak moment when Shambhu Nath Sen disagrees with the demeaning act of dowry during his daughter's handover. While narrating his own story, Anupam ironically reveals the account of that extraordinary event. When the wedding ceremony is almost ready, Shambhu Nath Sen's indifferent yet firm refusal, ignoring the worldly omen of the bride's misfortune at the last moment, signals the arrival of a new era. Through the awakening of a strong personality in a worker's role, the story concludes with Kalyani's pure and candid self-revelation, hinting at the arrival of the new woman of the future. 'Aporichita' is the story of a confession by a broken, personality-less young man filled with sorrow; it is through Anupam's sincere narration of his sins that the woman Kalyani in the story becomes extraordinary. The story not only depicts the inhumanity of patriarchy but also simultaneously praises women through a man's perspective.
---

To indicate the extent of his influence in the family, Anupam calls him the 'principal agent of the fate-goddess'. Read the following passage and answer questions 3 and 4\. Orphaned Deepu's uncle was the head of the family. Although Deepu was educated, he lacked the ability to make decisions. When his uncle took the initiative for his marriage and started negotiations involving dowry, visiting houses, the bride's father felt insulted and broke off the marriage talks. Although Deepu was captivated by the girl's picture, he couldn't say anything to his uncle. 3\) Which character in the 'Aporichita' story is similar to Deepu's uncle?
